## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the state variables are position x and velocity v, which is the standard phase-space form of a (possibly nonlinear, damped, and/or driven) oscillator. Typical models express dv_dt as a restoring force term depending on x plus optional damping terms depending on v and optional explicit time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation terms in t.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, small oscillations)
- Harmonic oscillator with constant bias: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shifted by constant force)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (damped oscillator with velocity-proportional drag)
- Time-dependent linear drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (externally driven damped oscillator)
- Cosine drive with phase: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t + c4) (forced response with phase shift)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (nonlinear stiffness plus viscous damping)
- Pendulum (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) (nonlinear restoring torque; small-angle limit recovers -c*x)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (pendulum with viscous damping)
- Quadratic/aerodynamic damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * Abs(v) * v (drag proportional to speed squared)
- Nonlinear polynomial damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent dissipation beyond linear)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * (x**2 - c2) * v (self-excited oscillation with limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * (v**2 - c2) * v (self-excitation controlled by velocity amplitude)
- Parametric (Mathieu-type) excitation: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness, parametric resonance)
- Nonlinear coupling between x and v: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**2 * v - c2 * v (state-dependent damping or feedback)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative (energy-preserving) oscillator structure: dv_dt depends on x only (dv_dt = -dU(x)/dx), with U(x) often even in x (e.g., x**2, x**4) giving odd restoring force terms (x, x**3).
- Damping typically appears as terms odd in v (e.g., v, Abs(v)*v, v**3) so that it dissipates energy regardless of velocity sign.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: adding +x**3 in the restoring force changes frequency with amplitude; the sign of the x**3 coefficient distinguishes hardening vs softening behavior.
- Geometric nonlinearities often introduce trigonometric restoring forces (sin(c*x)), with small-amplitude Taylor limits recovering polynomial forces.
- Self-excited oscillations/limit cycles are suggested by state-dependent damping like (x**2 - c)*v or (v**2 - c)*v, which injects energy at small amplitude and dissipates at large amplitude.
- External forcing usually introduces explicit periodic t terms (sin(c*t), cos(c*t + phase)), producing resonance peaks and steady-state oscillations even with damping.
- Parametric excitation is indicated by time-varying stiffness multiplying x (e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x), leading to instability tongues and subharmonic responses.
- Nonlinear dissipation from fluid/aerodynamic drag tends to scale like Abs(v)*v, making decay rate amplitude-dependent (faster decay at higher speeds).

GT: -c0*beta*v - omega0**c1*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 56

GT is the fixed function of \((x,v)\):
\[
-0.59954989233168\,v\;-\;2.79522534599104\,x\,e^{-|x|}.
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) have **no constant offset**, (ii) be **linear in \(v\)** with coefficient \(-0.59954989233168\), and (iii) have an \(x\)-term exactly of the form \(K\,x\,\exp(c\,|x|)\) with \(c=-1\) and \(K=-2.79522534599104\). Any extra dependence on \(t\), \(\sin\), \(\cos\), \(\log\), higher powers, \(v^3\), \(v|v|\), etc. must be eliminable by setting its coefficient to 0.

Below, “can match” means we can choose candidate constants to make it exactly the GT for all real \(x,v,t\).

---

### 1. \(c0 + c1 v + c2 x e^{c3|x|} + c4\sin(\cdots)\)
Set \(c0=0\), \(c4=0\). Then choose \(c1=-0.59954989233168\), \(c3=-1\), \(c2=-2.79522534599104\). **Matches.**

### 2. \(c0 + c1 v + c2 x e^{c3|x|} + c4 v + c5\log(\cdots)\)

### 3. \(c0 + c1 v + c2 x e^{c3|x|} + c4\sin(c5 t+c6)\)

### 4. \(c0 x + c1 + c2 v + c3 x^3 + c4 x^{c5} + c6 x e^{c7|x|}\)
